30:1085:66646:20:20:90:517:119:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the woman works and for all valuesat+1> a∗t+1the woman does not work int+ 1.  We
30:1086:66726:20:0:90:518:99:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:numerically check both the concavity of the conditional value functions and the uniqueness
31:1087:66818:0:21:90:518:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the reservation asset level.  The existence of this unique reservation asset level allows us
31:1088:66913:21:20:90:515:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to interpolate across the asset grid fort+ 1 since each level ofat+1is now associated with
31:1089:67003:20:20:90:431:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a participation decision att+ 1 and thus with a concave value function.
31:1090:67074:20:21:106:515:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:At this point, and conditional on marital status and the woman’s participation decision
31:1091:67161:21:20:90:515:609:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:at timet, we solve for the household’s optimal level of asset accumulation.  The option
31:1092:67248:20:20:90:518:589:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(work vs not work) which implies the highest utility then yields the LFP decision.  After
31:1093:67337:20:21:90:516:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:solving for all asset levels and participation decision for all possible states of nature and
31:1094:67430:21:20:90:516:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:marital status, the value functions in the married vs. divorce state are compared for each
31:1095:67520:20:43:90:476:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:agent and a marriage or divorce decision is given at each point of the state space.
31:1096:67603:43:32:90:373:485:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5  Implications of the Calibrated Model
31:1097:67642:32:20:90:530:453:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In this section we discuss the results obtained from the calibrationand examine the implications
31:1098:67738:20:36:90:344:433:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of different divorce regimes for married women’s LFP.
31:1099:67791:36:27:90:338:397:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.1  Model Fit and Calibrated Parameters
31:1100:67831:27:21:90:515:370:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:As can be seen from table 2, the model does a good job matching the data moments used
31:1101:67916:21:20:90:517:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the calibration.  It does an excellent job of reproducing the averages values of women’s
31:1102:68007:20:20:90:518:329:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:LFP, by marital status and conditional on having no children, childrenbelow the age of
31:1103:68093:20:21:90:516:309:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:5, and children between the ages of 5-10.  It also matches the conditional marriage and
31:1104:68180:21:20:90:517:288:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:divorce statistics extremely well.  The largest discrepancy is inmatching the divorce rate
31:1105:68270:20:20:90:517:268:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:during the ages of 35-44 and the immediate remarriage rate upon divorce over the ages
31:1106:68355:20:21:90:435:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:20-34, missing them by a bit over 1 and 2 percentage points respectively.
31:1107:68428:21:20:106:515:227:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The model also does well in generating some moments that were not directly targeted
31:1108:68511:20:20:90:516:207:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the calibration.  For example, conditional upon divorcing between the ages of 20-34, the
31:1109:68602:20:21:90:519:187:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:probability of remarrying within 20 years is 79.4% in the data versus 80.4% in the model.
31:1110:68691:21:20:90:516:166:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Furthermore, as can be seen in figure 2, the model also does a fairly goodjob in reproducing
31:1111:68783:20:20:90:516:146:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the general life-cycle profile of married and divorced women’s LFP, not just the targeted
31:1112:68872:20:21:90:226:126:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:averages across the life-cycle.
31:1113:68903:21:0:106:518:105:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Table 3 reports the values of the internally calibrated parameters.  A few comments
32:1114:68988:0:21:90:516:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are worth making.  First, note that the mean of the initialqdraw is higher for “young”
32:1115:69074:21:20:89:516:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:marriages than for “old” ones.  This is driven by the need to match the largeproportion
32:1116:69161:20:20:89:516:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of marriages that occur at young ages despite the fact that earnings are lowerand fertility
32:1117:69252:20:21:89:517:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is higher, both factors contributing to decrease consumption.  One way of thinking about
32:1118:69340:21:20:89:517:609:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:this is that individuals obtain pleasure from the prospect of having children and that this
32:1119:69431:20:20:89:516:589:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is captured in the higher mean ofqyoung.  Another important parameter governing the
32:1120:69514:20:21:89:515:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:evolution of love over time is the mean of the love shocks.  For marriagesformed when
32:1121:69599:21:20:89:517:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:young or when old, this parameter is positive and approximately 7 (young)to 8.5 (old)
32:1122:69684:20:20:89:519:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:percent of the initial value of the mean of the initial love draw.  Thisimplies thatqwill
32:1123:69773:20:21:89:462:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tend to increase by this percent each period over the duration of the marriage.
32:1124:69852:21:20:106:516:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Second, it is worth noting that, conditional on the age of a woman’s children, the
32:1125:69934:20:20:89:517:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:disutility of working is always higher for married women than for divorced ones.  In order
32:1126:70024:20:21:89:518:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to understand the magnitudes of these parameters, it is useful to state them in terms of
32:1127:70112:21:20:89:516:426:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:their consumption equivalence using the same consumption level.  To do this we compute
32:1128:70198:20:20:89:516:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the proportional decrease in average married consumption that a woman wouldbe willing
32:1129:70283:20:21:89:519:386:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to bear for one period in order to avoid incurring the disutility cost of working one period,
32:1130:70376:21:36:89:220:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:i.e., we find theξsksuch that
32:1131:70405:36:37:231:380:329:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:A:u((1−ξsk)cM) =u(cM)−ψsf(k)
32:1132:70431:37:20:89:517:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:wherecMis the average per-period consumption of a married agent (where the average is
32:1133:70516:20:21:90:517:272:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:taken over all married women across all model periods). The results ofthis calculation are
32:1134:70606:21:20:90:516:251:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:reported in Table 5 for allsandk, and range from 3.4 to 8.8 percent of average per-period
32:1135:70695:20:20:90:191:231:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:married consumption.
32:1136:70715:20:21:106:517:211:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:A similar exercise can be conducted to measure the psychic cost of divorce Φ. We solve
32:1137:70801:21:37:90:381:190:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for the consumption equivalence of Φ by solving forξΦbelow:
32:1138:70860:37:36:239:372:153:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:A:u((1−ξΦ)cM) =u(cM)−Φ
32:1139:70880:36:21:89:517:117:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We findξΦ= 0.192, i.e., individuals would be willing to sacrifice 19.2 percent of average
32:1140:70969:21:0:89:517:96:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:per-period married consumption (for one period) in order to avoid the psychic distress
33:1141:71057:0:21:90:516:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:associated with divorce.   We can also compare this number to the mean value of the
33:1142:71140:21:20:90:518:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:initial love draw when young,-youngq. The latter is smaller in magnitude (0.72 versus 1.49,
33:1143:71231:20:20:89:517:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:respectively) than the psychic cost of divorce; it is equivalent to 16.3 percent of average
33:1144:71322:20:37:90:244:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:per-period married consumption.
33:1145:71353:37:27:90:247:593:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.2  Married Women’s LFP
33:1146:71377:27:20:90:518:566:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:How does women’s LFP react to different divorce regimes?34To study these implications,
33:1147:71463:20:21:89:515:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:we generate the paths of women’s LFP under both divorce systems separately.  In both
33:1148:71547:21:20:89:517:525:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:cases, the regime remains in force throughout the agents’ entire lifecycle.  Figure 3 depicts
33:1149:71640:20:20:89:517:505:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the life-cycle profile of women’s LFP under the two pure divorce regimes (MCandU) as
33:1150:71724:20:21:90:518:485:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:well as in the benchmark model, for married women and, separately, for divorced women.
33:1151:71810:21:20:90:519:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The solid line with squares labeled LFPMCshows the LFP path under a regime of mutual
33:1152:71894:20:20:89:517:444:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consent divorce.  The solid line with triangles labeled LFPUis the LFP path under the
33:1153:71979:20:21:89:518:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:unilateral regime. Lastly, the dashed line is the LFP path obtained in the benchmark model
33:1154:72069:21:20:89:236:403:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:with its mix of divorce regimes.
33:1155:72101:20:20:106:519:383:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Note that the benchmark model’s LFP path coincides with the path undermutual
33:1156:72177:20:21:89:519:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consent through period 3 since the change in divorce regime in period4 in the benchmark is,
33:1157:72268:21:20:89:517:342:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:by assumption, unexpected. Thereafter, LFP is on average 1.5 percentage points higher per
33:1158:72357:20:20:89:516:322:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:period over the next 6 periods for married women in the benchmark model (now governed
33:1159:72442:20:21:89:518:302:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:by the unilateral divorce system).35Thus, the unexpected change in regime from mutual
33:1160:72527:21:20:89:499:281:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consent to unilateral increased married women’s LFP but not by a very large amount.
33:1161:72610:20:20:112:516:261:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We can compare the results above with those obtained by Stevenson (2008) using
33:1162:72688:20:16:89:517:241:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a variety of specifications.   First, using a simple differences-in-differences strategy that
33:1163:72781:16:15:98:517:225:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:34In an earlier paper (Fern ́andez and Wong (2013)) we examined howa largeexogenousincrease in the
33:1164:72879:15:11:90:516:210:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:probability of divorce affected married woman’s LFP.  We found thatdoubling the divorce rate increased
33:1165:72981:11:11:90:518:199:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:married women’s LFP increased significantly.   The modeling strategy used there had some advantages
33:1166:73080:11:11:90:518:188:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:and some disadvantages.  On the positive side, keeping marital status exogenous allowed us to consider
33:1167:73182:11:11:90:518:177:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:the interplay of several factors that otherwise are computationally very burdensome (e.g., the endogenous
33:1168:73287:11:11:90:518:166:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:accumulation of labor market experience). On the negative side, treating divorce probabilities as exogenous
33:1169:73394:11:11:90:516:155:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:meant that all the causality went in one direction – from greater divorce risk to higher LFP – rather than
33:1170:73500:11:11:90:517:144:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:allowing the two to interact.  The model ofendogenousmarital status in this paper allows us to make
33:1171:73599:11:11:90:517:133:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:greater headway in understanding the relationship between thedual transformation of women’s work and
33:1172:73699:11:7:90:188:122:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:the stability of marriage.
33:1173:73725:7:14:98:517:115:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:35The LFP of divorced women is also higher as a result of the change, but the increase is smaller – on
33:1174:73827:14:0:90:341:101:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:average less than 1 percentage point per period over 6 periods.
34:1175:73892:0:21:90:515:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:compared the change in married women’s LFP from 1970 to 1980 across states that changed
34:1176:73979:21:20:90:516:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:their divorce regime from mutual to unilateral versus those that did not, Stevenson found
34:1177:74068:20:20:90:519:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:an increase of about 1.5 percentage points associated with the unilateral regime.  Second,
34:1178:74158:20:21:90:528:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:running a Probit on married women’s LFP using individual controls and including time-varying
34:1179:74250:21:20:90:516:609:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:state policies (in addition to state and year fixed effects), she found that unilateral divorce
34:1180:74345:20:20:90:516:589:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is associated with around a 1.4 percentage points increase in the LFP of non-black married
34:1181:74435:20:21:90:516:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:women.  We can compare these results with those produced by our modelby calculating
34:1182:74518:21:20:90:516:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:LFPbenchmark- LFPMCin 1980 for married women. We obtain an increase of 2.7 percentage
34:1183:74603:20:20:90:346:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:points, which is in the same ballpark as her estimates.
34:1184:74658:20:21:106:519:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Turning next to the two pure divorce regimes, as can be seen from figure 3, the model
34:1185:74743:21:20:90:517:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:predicts that LFP, especially of married women, would have been substantially higher under
34:1186:74833:20:20:90:516:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a unilateral divorce regime. In particular, over the ages of 20-29 which iswhen most women
34:1187:74923:20:21:90:517:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are having children, it would have been 8.43 percentage points greateron average. Over the
34:1188:75013:21:20:90:515:426:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:first 5 periods (ages 20-44), it would have averaged 7 percentage points moreeach period
34:1189:75101:20:20:90:517:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:than under mutual consent.  When married women become older, the inequality changes
34:1190:75184:20:21:90:519:386:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sign and they would work a bit less under a unilateral divorce regime than under mutual
34:1191:75271:21:20:90:132:365:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:consent.36
34:1192:75281:20:20:111:516:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Table 4 reports several key LFP moments.  For ease of comparison, the first column
34:1193:75363:20:21:89:517:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:replicates the benchmark results, and the second and third columnscompare the two pure
34:1194:75449:21:20:89:518:304:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:divorce regimes. Note that the overall ratio of female to male wages is lower under unilateral
34:1195:75543:20:20:89:517:284:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:than under mutual consent as a greater proportion of lower-productivity women enter the
34:1196:75630:20:21:89:206:264:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:labor force in the former.
34:1197:75656:21:20:106:516:243:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:What mechanism drives the large difference in married women’s LFP over the two
34:1198:75734:20:20:89:517:223:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:regimes?  It may be easiest to start by ruling out certain explanations.  First, note that
34:1199:75824:20:21:89:516:203:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:there are no returns to experience in this model – wages are assumedto automatically
34:1200:75908:21:20:89:518:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:increase with age.  Hence, the desire to accumulate more labor market experience cannot
34:1201:75995:20:16:89:517:162:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:be playing a role.37Second, it is also worth noting that the increase cannot be the result
34:1202:76085:16:15:98:517:146:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:36It would be interesting to examine whether this result holds in the data.  It is not an easy exercise to
34:1203:76191:15:11:90:517:131:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:conduct, however, as it would require contrasting the LFP of married women who always expected to live
34:1204:76293:11:11:90:516:120:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:under each of the two divorce regimes.  One possibility could beto examine the LFP for married women
34:1205:76393:11:7:90:461:109:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:20-30 years old under each regime (i.e., differentiating across states), sample size permitting.
34:1206:76489:7:0:98:519:102:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:37In our earlier paper (Fern ́andez and Wong (2013)), we found thatthe endogenous accumulation of
35:1207:76588:0:21:90:515:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of a strategic calculation in which women work more in order to decrease the probability
35:1208:76676:21:20:90:516:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that their husbands will want to divorce them.  Nor can it be the outcome ofa “contract”
35:1209:76764:20:20:90:516:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in which wives agree to increase family income and husbands agree to a lower probability
35:1210:76852:20:21:90:517:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of divorce.  The timing of decisions within a period effectively rules out these possibilities
35:1211:76946:21:20:90:515:609:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as first individuals make marital status decisions and only subsequently does the household
35:1212:77037:20:20:90:517:589:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:make work and savings decisions.38Thus married women’s LFP must be optimal (in the
35:1213:77119:20:21:89:519:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sense of maximizing the weighted sum of spouses’ utilities)taking as giventhe marital
35:1214:77204:21:20:89:161:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:status outcome.
35:1215:77219:20:20:106:517:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Why then do married women work more under a unilateral divorce regime?To answer
35:1216:77298:20:21:89:516:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:this we need to understand how an (endogenously) higher divorce riskaffects married
35:1217:77381:21:20:89:519:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:agents’ preferences over their other endogenous outcomes: work, consumption, and savings.
35:1218:77470:20:20:89:518:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Consider a married household in which the wife did not work.  Divorce has two important
35:1219:77557:20:21:89:516:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:effects: it changes the size of each spouse’s household and it divides marital assets (assume
35:1220:77650:21:20:89:516:426:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:50-50).  From a man’s perspective, the first effect is large as he goes from supporting a
35:1221:77739:20:20:89:516:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:family of, say, 4 to supporting only himself (and transferring 10 percent of his income to
35:1222:77829:20:21:89:516:386:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:his ex-spouse).  From the woman’s perspective, she goes from a familyof 4 to a family
35:1223:77914:21:20:89:517:365:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:of 3 and must now support it on labor income that is 30 percent smaller on average.39
35:1224:77999:20:20:89:519:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Thus, consumption smoothing implies that in face of higher divorce risk, married men will
35:1225:78088:20:21:89:516:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:want to borrow more (or save less) than their wives.   The solution to these conflicting
35:1226:78176:21:20:89:517:304:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:preferences is governed by the relative Pareto weight on spouses’ preferences (which favors
35:1227:78267:20:20:89:515:284:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:men). However, rather than savings bearing the entire required adjustment, another option
35:1228:78356:20:21:89:515:264:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is for the married woman to enter the labor force.  Doing so increases men’s welfare (and
35:1229:78445:21:20:89:516:243:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:decreases women’s) but, by allowing savings to fall less, it can be asuperior solution to the
35:1230:78538:20:20:89:242:223:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:household optimization problem.
35:1231:78569:20:20:106:516:203:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:To illustrate the reasoning above, table 6 reports the average assets held by married
35:1232:78654:20:11:90:517:183:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:experience was not a significant contributor to the increase in married women’s LFP when confronted with
35:1233:78758:11:7:90:210:172:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:a doubling of the divorce rate.
35:1234:78789:7:15:98:516:165:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:38This timing is the one required by our assumption of the inability to commit to actionscontingentupon
35:1235:78892:15:11:90:518:150:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:a certain marital status.  In the future it may be interesting to explore the consequences of alternative
35:1236:78997:11:11:90:516:139:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:timing assumptions in which individuals can make labor force participation decisions simultaneously with
35:1237:79101:11:11:90:519:128:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:marital status decisions, i.e., essentially they can committo working in that period. In this paper, however,
35:1238:79210:11:7:90:365:117:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:we are interested in exploring fully the non-commitment assumption.
35:1239:79277:7:15:98:519:110:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:39The average consumption of a divorced woman in the model ranges from 57 percent to 66 percent of
35:1240:79375:15:0:90:292:95:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:the divorce man’s consumption, depending on age.
36:1241:79425:0:21:90:517:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:couples and the average LFP of married women in each period under the mutual consent
36:1242:79509:21:20:90:517:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:versus the unilateral divorce regimes.  Columns 3 and 6 present the difference in the levels
36:1243:79601:20:20:90:516:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of these variables between the two divorce systems. As can be seen inthe table, relative to
36:1244:79692:20:21:90:516:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a mutual consent regime, savings are lower (borrowing increases) andLFP is significantly
36:1245:79780:21:20:90:517:609:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:higher over the first four periods of life under a unilateral regime.Thereafter saving starts
36:1246:79873:20:20:90:416:589:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to increase as retirement incentives kick in and women’s LFP drops.
36:1247:79940:20:21:106:515:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Of course, the composition of married agents differs across divorce regime.   Could
36:1248:80023:21:20:89:517:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:selection be responsible for most of the increase in married women’s LFP obtained under
36:1249:80110:20:20:89:516:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the unilateral divorce regime?   To check this possibility, for each period we divide the
36:1250:80199:20:21:89:518:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:population of married women into quintiles ofztusing the distribution of couples that
36:1251:80284:21:20:89:516:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:period under mutual consent.  We do the same for married men.  This yields a 5x5 matrix
36:1252:80371:20:20:89:517:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of married couples. For each cell we can calculate women’s LFP under the mutual consent
36:1253:80458:20:21:89:518:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:regime vs the unilateral divorce regime.  Using the same weights per cell as under mutual
36:1254:80547:21:20:89:516:426:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consent (at timet) allows us to eliminate the effect of differential selection into marriage
36:1255:80639:20:20:90:282:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on married women’s LFP in that period.
36:1256:80677:20:21:106:517:386:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We find that selection plays a role in the increase in married women’sLFP but that it
36:1257:80762:21:20:90:515:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is significantly less important than the increased motivation to work faced by all married
36:1258:80852:20:20:90:519:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:women.40For example, had the distribution of couples remained the same as in mutual
36:1259:80935:20:21:89:516:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consent, then married women’s LFP would have increased from 35.80 percent to 43.83
36:1260:81017:21:20:89:512:304:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:percent rather than to 45.22 percent in period 1.  In period 2 it would have increased from
36:1261:81108:20:20:89:516:284:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:39.25 to 45.58 rather than to 46.68.  Thus, in the first two periods selection into marriage
36:1262:81200:20:21:89:514:264:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is responsible for 15.8 percent and 14.8 percent, respectively, of the total increase in LFP
36:1263:81292:21:16:89:272:243:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:induced by a unilateral divorce regime.
36:1264:81331:16:14:98:517:227:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:40We also checked, using the same methodology, whether the results regarding savings was driven by
36:1265:81429:14:11:90:516:213:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:differential selection into marriage.  They are not.  For example, had the distribution of couples remained
36:1266:81536:11:11:90:517:202:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:the same as in mutual consent, then average assets would have decreased from -5.46 to -6.42 rather than to
36:1267:81642:11:11:90:516:191:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:-6.75 in period 1.  In period 2 it would have decreased from -6.55 to-7.72 rather than to -8.06.  Thus, in
36:1268:81748:11:11:90:519:180:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:the first two periods selection into marriage is responsible for 25.0 percent and 22.4 percent, respectively, of
36:1269:81860:11:0:90:390:169:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:the total decrease in married assets induced by a unilateral divorce regime.
37:1270:81938:0:32:90:369:691:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:6  Welfare Analysis of Divorce Regimes
37:1271:81976:32:20:90:517:659:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Prior to the welfare analysis it is useful to summarize the consequences of each regime for
37:1272:82067:20:20:90:517:639:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:several key marital status moments and to understand how each affects agents’ preferences
37:1273:82156:20:36:90:173:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:towards marriage.
37:1274:82173:36:28:90:454:583:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:6.1  The Impact of Divorce Regimes on Marriage and Divorce
37:1275:82231:28:20:90:516:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We start by examining how divorce regimes affect the basic marital moments.   These
37:1276:82314:20:20:90:517:535:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are reported in table 7.  For ease of comparison, the first column replicatesthe numbers
37:1277:82402:20:21:90:518:515:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from the benchmark model.  As can be seen in the table, relative to a regime of mutual
37:1278:82488:21:20:90:517:494:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consent, unilateral divorce slightly more than doubles the divorce rate while younger (ages
37:1279:82579:20:20:90:517:474:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:20-34) and generates an increase of over 30% in the proportion of marriages that divorce
37:1280:82667:20:21:90:516:454:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:when older (ages 35-44).  Women are significantly less likely to marry whileyounger with
37:1281:82755:21:20:90:516:433:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the marriage rate decreasing over 14 percentage points, a 16% decrease.  They are also
37:1282:82841:20:20:90:516:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:somewhat more likely to marry when older: 4.4% versus 4.0%.  The proportionof women
37:1283:82924:20:21:90:517:393:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:who remarry within five years (conditional on having divorced when younger) remains
37:1284:83007:21:20:90:517:372:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:fairly constant across regimes. The average (truncated) time spent divorced when younger
37:1285:83095:20:20:90:517:352:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:increases somewhat.  The marriage gap between higher and lower income mennarrows
37:1286:83175:20:21:90:519:332:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and the divorce gap widens (becoming more negative under unilateral thanunder mutual
37:1287:83259:21:20:90:130:311:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consent).
37:1288:83268:20:20:106:518:291:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We next turn to an analysis of the mechanisms that produce these results and their
37:1289:83350:20:21:89:517:271:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ultimate welfare implications.  How does the freedom to walk away fromone’s spouse
37:1290:83432:21:20:89:517:250:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:affect welfare? For any individual and a given pattern of marriages, evaluating the welfare
37:1291:83523:20:20:89:515:230:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consequences of a unilateral versus a mutual consent regime requires weighing the expected
37:1292:83613:20:21:89:518:210:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:benefit of those states of nature in which she/he wishes to be free to walk away from her/his
37:1293:83706:21:20:89:516:189:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:spouse without compensating the latter, against the expected cost of the reverse – being
37:1294:83794:20:20:89:350:169:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the one walked out on without receiving compensation.
37:1295:83847:20:21:106:516:149:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:It is clear why,for a given pattern of marriages, the winners from a unilateral regime
37:1296:83933:21:20:89:516:128:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:relative to mutual consent should be men on average.   Divorce is less costly for men
37:1297:84018:20:0:89:517:108:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:since they earn substantially more than women on average and also bear a smaller share
38:1298:84106:0:21:90:517:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the cost of raising children upon divorce.  The benefits of marriage tend to be smaller
38:1299:84196:21:20:90:521:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for men as well.  Although both spouses gain equally from the quality of the match,q,
38:1300:84281:20:20:89:517:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:other costs and benefits are not equal.  On the positive side, both spouses obtain some
38:1301:84368:20:21:89:517:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:insurance from marriage: a man’s wife is more likely to work if he is hitby a negative
38:1302:84454:21:20:89:518:609:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:income shock. Moreover, marriage provides a woman with an additional (or sole) source of
38:1303:84542:20:20:89:516:589:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:income that is on average substantially higher than hers.  On the negativeside, marriage
38:1304:84630:20:21:89:518:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tends to substantially decrease a man’s consumption, especially ifhis wife doesn’t work.
38:1305:84718:21:20:89:517:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:It may also decrease a woman’s consumption, depending on family size,but this effect
38:1306:84802:20:20:89:518:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is smaller than in the case of the man, given relative wages.  Lastly, marriageincreases
38:1307:84890:20:21:89:518:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a woman’s disutility from working (normalized at zero when single), especially if she has
38:1308:84979:21:20:89:516:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:children.  Thus, while marriage is not a bad deal for either men or women -after all, they
38:1309:85069:20:20:89:517:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are choosing to get married – upon receiving a negative match quality shock, it is more
38:1310:85156:20:36:89:511:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:likely that the husband will be the one to benefit from the ability toexit at a lower cost.
38:1311:85247:36:27:89:354:411:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f8:C:The median agent and marital status preferences
38:1312:85294:27:21:89:517:384:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:To better illustrate the points made above (and no longer keeping constant marriage
38:1313:85377:21:20:89:517:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:patterns across divorce regimes), we can trace out the evolution of two cutoff levels: the
38:1314:85467:20:20:89:517:343:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:minimumqrequired in order to desire to marry assuming that in each period the agent is
38:1315:85553:20:21:89:516:323:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:single (and has been in the past), and the minimumqrequired to desire to stay married
38:1316:85638:21:20:89:517:302:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(i.e., to not want a divorce) assuming the agent is married (and has beenin the past).  We
38:1317:85728:20:20:89:435:282:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:denote these minimums byqMg,minand byqDg,min, respectively,g∈ {f,m}.
38:1318:85796:20:21:106:516:262:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We perform theqsg,mincalculations for an agent endowed with the medianz0and with
38:1319:85876:21:20:89:517:241:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a marital typeez′0,whereez′0equals the expected value of the match the median agent
38:1320:85959:20:20:89:517:221:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:would obtain, i.e,ez′0=E(z′0|z0).  We assume that a single agent faces in each period the
38:1321:86048:20:21:89:516:201:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:distribution of future draws associated with ΩSt−1(e.g., the innovations inztandz′t, etc) and
38:1322:86141:21:20:89:515:180:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ex-post resolve the uncertainty in each period by setting the innovations to their expected
38:1323:86232:20:20:89:515:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:values.  This implies that in the following period the single agent is again endowed with
38:1324:86321:20:21:89:512:140:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the medianzt(recall thatE(ǫy) = 0) and her/his marital type’s productivity isE(z′t|ez′0).
38:1325:86410:21:20:106:520:119:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Similarly, we assume that a married agent faces the future distribution of draws associated
38:1326:86501:20:0:90:515:99:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:with ΩMt−1and ex post resolve the uncertainty by setting all innovations to their expected
39:1327:86593:0:21:90:517:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:values.  Thus the following period the married agent has the medianztand the spouse has
39:1328:86680:21:20:90:515:670:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f3:B:E(z′t|ez′0).  Since ex-post fertility must be an integer, we set the realization to one child in
39:1329:86776:20:20:90:517:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the first period and to an additional child in the second period. We also assume that this is
39:1330:86869:20:21:90:517:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the married agents’ first marriage.  For both single and married agents, assets evolve over
39:1331:86960:21:20:90:516:609:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:time as prescribed by the solutions to the optimization problems (as described in section
39:1332:87049:20:20:90:108:589:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:3.2).
39:1333:87054:20:21:106:517:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Table 8 presents the evolution ofqsg,minover time.  The entries on the left side of the
39:1334:87141:21:20:90:517:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:table report the values ofqMg,min(for single agents) andqDg,min(for married agents) under the
39:1335:87234:20:20:90:517:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:mutual consent regime; those on the right correspond to the unilateral regime.  The lower
39:1336:87323:20:21:90:517:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:panel translates the cutoff values into potential “acceptance” rates – the proportion of the
39:1337:87415:21:20:90:517:487:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:B:qdistribution that is not rejected or that does not end in divorce. For asingle agent this is
39:1338:87508:20:20:90:518:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:equivalent to the proportion of the matches that she/he would want to become marriages.
39:1339:87595:20:21:90:516:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:For a married agent, the proportion of acceptances is not conditioned on the fact that being
39:1340:87687:21:20:90:517:426:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:married in periodt−1 implies thatqt−1must have fallen in a certain range.  Hence, the
39:1341:87772:20:20:90:517:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:“acceptance” rate reported is not the complement of the divorce rate – itsimply provides
39:1342:87860:20:21:90:517:386:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:an indication of how the preferences of agents evolve over time and by gender.  Lastly, to
39:1343:87950:21:20:90:515:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:facilitate comparisons, we calculateqDg,minunder the assumption that divorce in that period
39:1344:88041:20:20:90:516:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:would split marital assets equally. This assumption allows us to illustrate the difference in
39:1345:88134:20:21:90:519:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:women’s and men’s valuation of marriage prior to any compensation required under mutual
39:1346:88221:21:20:90:132:304:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:consent.41
39:1347:88231:20:20:106:515:284:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Some interesting patterns that are common to both divorce regimes can bediscerned
39:1348:88312:20:21:90:517:264:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from table 8. First, single women and men both become less choosy about marital partners
39:1349:88400:21:20:90:519:243:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as time progresses. Two factors are mainly responsible for this: the possibility that they will
39:1350:88495:20:20:90:516:223:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:have more than one child falls (which lowers the consumption cost of marriage as well as the
39:1351:88587:20:21:90:519:203:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:number of periods with high disutility of work) and (potential) earnings increase.  Second,
39:1352:88678:21:20:90:517:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:note that initially single women are choosier than single men; this pattern reverses at age
39:1353:88769:20:20:90:517:162:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:30-34.  At that point single women become less concerned about the negative economic
39:1354:88853:20:16:90:516:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consequences of children within marriage and also less concerned aboutexiting a marriage
39:1355:88941:16:15:98:519:126:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:41If mutual consent were required, there would be only oneqDminfor the couple as they must both agree.
39:1356:89043:15:11:90:519:111:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:Note that the assumption of an equal split is only made for the current period; agents under a mutual
39:1357:89144:11:0:90:371:100:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:consent regime assume that in future periods consent will be required.
40:1358:89216:0:21:90:277:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:under negative economic circumstances.
40:1359:89254:21:20:106:517:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:One may ask why single women living under a mutual consent regime should care about
40:1360:89337:20:20:89:518:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the possibility that once they marry they may eventually divorce.   After all, they will
40:1361:89425:20:21:89:517:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:be compensated in that event.  There are two reasons.  First, compensation only leaves
40:1362:89511:21:20:89:517:609:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:women indifferent between marriage and divorce.  When staying in a marriage becomes
40:1363:89594:20:20:89:518:589:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:unattractive (either because the man’s wages are low or because the match quality is low),
40:1364:89684:20:21:89:516:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the amount of compensation a woman receives is also likely low.  Second, even when being
40:1365:89772:21:20:89:517:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:married is unattractive to both parties, a husband may not be able to afford to make his
40:1366:89860:20:20:89:517:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:wife indifferent between divorce and marriage, and thus the couple remains married. While
40:1367:89949:20:21:89:515:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:this makes a woman better off than being divorced, it is still not a statethat she would
40:1368:90037:21:20:89:401:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:prefer relative to remaining single and waiting for a better match.
40:1369:90104:20:20:106:518:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:It is worth remarking that the model is able to capture several well-known features of
40:1370:90190:20:21:89:515:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:mate preferences.  Basic evolutionary theory predicts that females should be choosier than
40:1371:90280:21:20:89:519:426:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:males since the former invest more in their young.  This result is generated in the model
40:1372:90369:20:20:89:517:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as a result of children being more costly to a woman.  The finding that the inequality is
40:1373:90458:20:21:89:517:386:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:reversed over time, with single men becoming choosier than singlewomen, seems at least
40:1374:90544:21:20:89:166:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:anecdotally true.
40:1375:90561:20:20:106:517:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Next, note that married men are more willing to divorce than married women.  This
40:1376:90642:20:21:89:517:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is due to the various gender asymmetries previous discussed: men earn more on average
40:1377:90727:21:20:89:517:304:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and bear a smaller share of the cost of raising children.  Interestingly, the pattern over
40:1378:90817:20:20:89:517:284:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:time ofqDg,mindiffers by gender.  It is monotonically decreasing for men, indicatingthat as
40:1379:90908:20:21:90:516:264:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:they age they become less inclined to divorce.  For women, on the other hand, theqDf,min
40:1380:90996:21:20:90:517:243:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:follows an inverted U shape.  Married women’s willingness to divorcepeaks during ages
40:1381:91081:20:20:90:516:223:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:30-34 and then decreases.  There are many things happening simultaneously that change
40:1382:91166:20:21:90:516:203:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the attractiveness of marriage relative to divorce over time for women but it seems that the
40:1383:91258:21:20:90:517:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:relative attractiveness of marriage increases with the growth in the husband’s labor income
40:1384:91349:20:20:90:173:162:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:over the life cycle.
40:1385:91369:20:21:106:517:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Comparing next across regimes, note from table 8 that, indeed, the minimumqsingle
40:1386:91450:21:20:90:517:121:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:women require in order to marry is higher under the unilateral divorce regime than under
40:1387:91538:20:0:90:518:101:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:mutual consent, indicating their greater reluctance to be married in a unilateral system.
41:1388:91629:0:21:90:516:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:This is because marriage without compensation for divorce is less attractive to women since
41:1389:91720:21:20:90:516:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:they will more often find themselves being walked out on rather than being the ones who
41:1390:91807:20:20:90:517:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:walk away.42The minimumqrequired for a woman to remain married is also higher under
41:1391:91890:20:21:90:515:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the unilateral system since the lower value of marriage makes it less attractive to stay in
41:1392:91981:21:20:90:519:609:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a low quality marriage.  For single men, on the other hand,qMm,minfalls relative to mutual
41:1393:92071:20:20:89:517:589:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consent indicating the greater attractiveness of marriage for them now that the exit cost
41:1394:92160:20:21:89:517:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is lower.  For married men,qDm,minalso falls since the value of marriage has increased for
41:1395:92250:21:20:89:518:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:them. To understand why men are more eager to be divorced under mutualconsent, recall
41:1396:92335:20:20:89:516:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that the calculation we performed to obtainqDm,minallowed agents, only in that period, to
41:1397:92424:20:21:89:516:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:exit the marriage without compensating their spouse.43This caused some men to “jump”
41:1398:92508:21:20:89:519:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:at the opportunity of a relatively inexpensive divorce that period.Under the unilateral
41:1399:92595:20:20:89:515:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:regime, the opportunity to divorce without compensating one’s spousealways exists and
41:1400:92680:20:21:89:517:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:hence men are less eager to exit marriage and are consequently less demanding vis a vis
41:1401:92767:21:20:89:167:426:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:marriage quality.
41:1402:92784:20:20:106:517:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Overall, it is clear that the preferences of men and women vis a vis marriage move
41:1403:92866:20:21:89:517:386:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in opposite directions across regimes.  The net decrease in the marriagerate under the
41:1404:92952:21:20:89:517:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:unilateral regime allows one to conclude that women’s greater reluctance to marry prevails
41:1405:93042:20:20:89:516:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:over men’s greater willingness to marry.   Note that although marriage rates fall and
41:1406:93127:20:21:89:518:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:those that marriages that form have, on average, a higher value of the initiallove draw,
41:1407:93215:21:36:89:395:304:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:nevertheless a greater proportion of marriages end up in divorce.
41:1408:93280:36:27:89:391:268:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:6.2  The Welfare Consequences of Divorce Regimes
41:1409:93328:27:20:89:516:241:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:To study the overall welfare consequences of the two divorce regimes we perform two
41:1410:93411:20:21:89:518:221:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:calculations.  The first asks, conditional solely on gender, but otherwise under the “veil of
41:1411:93504:21:16:89:516:200:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ignorance”, whether women and men prefer one regime to the other. The second calculation
41:1412:93592:16:15:98:516:184:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:42The model predicts that under a unilateral divorce regime, men will be the ones who wish to divorce in
41:1413:93696:15:10:89:518:169:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:78 percent of the cases.  This figure is for the entire universe of agents between the ages of 25 to 44.  As
41:1414:93804:10:11:89:518:159:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:has been noted in the literature, these numbers are not comparablewith figures about who legally initiates
41:1415:93910:11:8:89:389:148:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:divorce as there exist other social considerations that influence this choice.
41:1416:93988:8:14:98:514:140:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:43This was for illustrative purposes only – i.e., to indicate howmuch men value marriage. If we forced them
41:1417:94095:14:11:89:517:126:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:to compensate their wives, as required under MC, then there would be no gender differences and, in some
41:1418:94198:11:11:89:516:115:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:casesqMm,minwould not be defined since marital assets would be insufficiently large to allow compensation
41:1419:94303:11:0:89:122:104:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:to occur.
42:1420:94314:0:21:90:517:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:delves deeper into the welfare consequences of divorce regimes byconditioning ex-ante
42:1421:94399:21:20:90:517:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:expected welfare not only on gender but also on the agent’s initial endowmentz0.  This
42:1422:94485:20:36:89:474:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:allows us to understand how preferences differ across poorer versus richer agents.
42:1423:94567:36:27:89:269:614:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f8:C:Ex Ante Welfare: Women vs Men
42:1424:94596:27:20:89:517:587:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Table 9 shows the results of both welfare calculations.  The first column (“All Quintiles”)
42:1425:94687:20:21:89:516:567:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:reports, for each divorce regime, the ex ante expected utility of an agent of genderg. As can
42:1426:94780:21:20:90:519:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:be easily seen, women prefer the mutual consent regime whereas men prefer the unilateral
42:1427:94868:20:20:90:516:526:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:divorce regime.  The third and sixth row provide a measure of the extent to which one
42:1428:94953:20:21:90:515:506:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:system is preferred to the other by reporting the percentageρby which the consumption
42:1429:95038:21:20:90:517:485:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of gendergwould have be increasedin each state of nature and in each time periodin the
42:1430:95124:20:20:90:516:465:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:mutual consent regime so as to leave that gender indifferent ex ante between the two divorce
42:1431:95216:20:21:90:223:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:regimes.44That is,ρsolves:
42:1432:95242:21:30:267:517:424:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:A:WMCg0(ρ) =WUg0(11)
42:1433:95260:30:20:90:516:394:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:whereWrg0is the expected utility, at timet= 0, of an agent of gendergin divorce regime
42:1434:95346:20:20:90:521:374:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:B:rwhosez0is unknown but is assumed to be a random draw from the initial (normal)
42:1435:95425:20:37:90:211:354:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:distributionh(z0. That is,
42:1436:95451:37:0:235:266:317:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:A:Wrg0=
42:1437:95456:0:25:269:275:332:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f15:C:Z
42:1438:95457:25:0:275:283:307:8:g_d0_f11:6:g_d0_f5:F:z0
42:1439:95459:0:37:286:517:317:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:A:EVrg0(z0)h(z0)dz0(12)
42:1440:95480:37:20:90:517:280:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:whereEVrg0(z0) is the expected utility of an agent of gendergat timet= 0 assuming that
42:1441:95566:20:21:90:517:260:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:her/his initial productivity draw wasz0.  Expectations are taken over all possible paths
42:1442:95654:21:20:89:518:239:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of shocks, marital decisions conditional on the shocks, and for each possible endowment of
42:1443:95744:20:20:89:244:219:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:potential spousal type givenz0.
42:1444:95775:20:20:106:515:199:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Note that, perhaps surprisingly, men’s preference for the unilateral regime is not very
42:1445:95862:20:21:89:518:179:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:strong: their consumption would need to be increased by only 1.25 percent under mutual
42:1446:95948:21:20:89:519:158:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consent in order to be indifferent.  Women, on the other hand, strongly prefer the mutual
42:1447:96037:20:20:89:516:138:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consent regime.  They would be willing to have their consumption decreased up to 15.76
42:1448:96123:20:16:89:514:118:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:percent under mutual consent in order not to live under a unilateraldivorce regime.  A
42:1449:96209:16:0:98:498:102:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:44Note that a negativeρimplies that the agent prefers the mutual consent regime to the unilateral.
43:1450:96309:0:21:90:517:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:significant part of this welfare calculation is driven by disutility from labor.  This can be
43:1451:96402:21:20:90:518:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:seen by keeping the outcomes the same under both regimes but ignoring(setting to zero)
43:1452:96488:20:20:90:517:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:women’s work disutility. The consumption decrease required to make women indifferent
43:1453:96572:20:36:90:336:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:between divorce regimes falls to 6.9 percent instead.
43:1454:96625:36:27:90:183:594:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f8:C:Political Economy
43:1455:96642:27:21:90:516:567:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:An interesting political economy question is whether a simple changesuch as a more
43:1456:96724:21:20:90:518:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:generous child support would persuade women, in an ex-ante sense, to favor a unilateral
43:1457:96811:20:20:90:516:526:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:system.  To answer this question we solve for the fraction of income thatmen would have
43:1458:96898:20:21:90:516:506:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to transfer to women in the form of child support so as to leave them indifferent between
43:1459:96987:21:20:90:518:485:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the two divorce systems.  This more generous transfer is received only in the unilateral
43:1460:97075:20:20:90:515:465:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:system; the mutual consent transfer remains constant at 10 percent as in the benchmark
43:1461:97161:20:21:90:517:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:model. We allow all decisions to change endogenously in response to thenew child-support
43:1462:97249:21:20:90:155:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:transfer value.
43:1463:97264:20:20:106:517:404:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We find that the childcare transfer would have to increase to 24.49 percent to leave
43:1464:97348:20:21:89:515:384:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:women indifferent between the two divorce regimes.  This change, however, leaves men
43:1465:97432:21:20:89:519:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:worse off under unilateral divorce than under the mutual consent regimewith the original
43:1466:97520:20:20:89:513:343:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:child support.  Thus, while such a change would garner women’s support, it would now
43:1467:97604:20:36:89:346:323:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:leave men favoring the mutual consent divorce regime.
43:1468:97657:36:27:89:279:287:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f8:C:Ex Ante Welfare: Rich versus Poor
43:1469:97690:27:21:89:516:260:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Next, we examine how preferences within gender depend on expected income by conditioning
43:1470:97778:21:20:89:517:239:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on the quintile of the initialzdraw (z0) in addition to gender.  Thus, ex ante, an agent
43:1471:97866:20:20:90:516:219:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:knows both gender and the quintile of her/hisz0.  Columns 2-6 report, by quintile, the ex
43:1472:97955:20:21:90:521:199:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:ante expected utility under each divorce regime for an agent of gendergendowed with az0
43:1473:98042:21:20:90:519:178:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that is a random draw from the indicated quintileQn,n∈ {1,2,...,5}of thez0distribution.
43:1474:98129:20:20:90:516:158:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:As before, in rows 3 and 6 we solve for the percentρby which consumption would need to
43:1475:98215:20:0:90:516:138:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:be increased under the mutual consent regime so as to leave the agent indifferent between
44:1476:98306:0:37:90:352:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the 2 divorce regimes.  That is, we solve forρsuch that
44:1477:98361:37:37:258:517:654:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:A:WMCg0,Qn(ρ) =WUg0,Qn(13)
44:1478:98385:37:20:90:113:617:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:where
44:1479:98390:20:0:220:264:597:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:A:Wrg0,Qn=
44:1480:98398:0:25:268:274:612:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f15:C:Z
44:1481:98399:25:0:274:299:587:8:g_d0_f11:6:g_d0_f14:F:z0∈Qn
44:1482:98404:0:30:302:517:597:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:A:EVrg0(z0)h(z0)dz0(14)
44:1483:98425:30:21:106:518:567:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:As is clear from Table 9, men born with initial productivity in the lowest two quintiles
44:1484:98513:21:20:89:517:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:prefer, on average, the mutual consent regime as do women with initial productivity in the
44:1485:98603:20:20:89:516:526:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:lowest three quintiles.  Higher productivity men and women prefer the unilateral divorce
44:1486:98691:20:21:89:517:506:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:system.  What explains these preference differences?  Overall, they stem from how the
44:1487:98776:21:20:89:516:485:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:valuation of the ability to exit a marriage easily vis a vis the consumption insurance offered
44:1488:98870:20:20:89:517:465:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:by a stable marriage differs with expected income.   Higher initial productivity agents
44:1489:98957:20:21:89:516:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:expect to earn more and thus they benefit less from the insurance provided by marriage
44:1490:99043:21:20:89:517:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:relative to the ability to easily leave a low quality marriage.  They are also more likely to
44:1491:99136:20:20:89:519:404:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:need to make greater compensations in order to divorce a spouse under mutual consent.
44:1492:99221:20:21:89:516:384:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Lower-income individuals value more the insurance benefits of marriageand are more likely
44:1493:99310:21:20:89:517:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to profit from compensation under mutual consent.  Reinforcing these motives is the fact
44:1494:99398:20:20:89:513:343:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that lower-income women are the agents that are worst hit by divorce.  This leads them
44:1495:99484:20:21:89:517:323:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to reject marriage more frequently, thus decreasing marriage formationand its insurance
44:1496:99571:21:20:89:517:302:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:benefits disproportionately for both lower-income men and women. It isinteresting to note
44:1497:99660:20:20:89:516:282:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that over the last few decades, this is precisely what has happened:white women with
44:1498:99744:20:21:89:516:262:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:college education marry with greater frequency than before whereas their lower-education
44:1499:99832:21:20:89:516:241:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:counterparts have seen a decrease in their probability of marrying (see, e.g., Stevenson and
44:1500:99924:20:43:89:146:221:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Isen (2010)).
44:1501:99937:43:31:89:181:178:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:7  Conclusion
44:1502:99950:31:21:89:517:147:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:This paper developed a quantitative dynamic life-cycle model of endogenous marital status
44:1503:100039:21:20:89:517:126:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to study the positive and normative consequences of two divorce regimes: mutual consent
44:1504:100126:20:0:89:519:106:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and unilateral divorce.  Our analysis is conducted in an environment of imperfect capital
45:1505:100217:0:21:90:516:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and insurance markets, and with very limited commitment ability other than that provided
45:1506:100305:21:20:90:518:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:by the legal system.  In this framework, marriage not only provides agentswith love, but
45:1507:100393:20:20:90:519:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:also with a degree of insurance against adverse income shocks. It simultaneously, however,
45:1508:100483:20:21:90:405:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:exposes them to other sources of uncertainty (e.g., match quality).
45:1509:100550:21:20:106:516:609:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We calibrated the model to key moments for the 1940 cohort which lived through both
45:1510:100633:20:20:89:517:589:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:divorce regimes.  Conditioning solely on gender, our ex ante welfare analysis found that
45:1511:100721:20:21:89:519:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:women would fare better under mutual consent whereas men would prefer a unilateral
45:1512:100803:21:20:89:515:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:system.  Once we condition on initial productivity by quintile as well as gender, we find
45:1513:100892:20:20:89:517:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that men in the top three quintiles of the initial productivity distribution would be made
45:1514:100982:20:21:89:515:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:better off by a unilateral system as would the top two quintiles of women; the rest would
45:1515:101071:21:20:89:515:487:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:prefer mutual consent. These results can be explained by two gender asymmetries: women
45:1516:101157:20:20:89:518:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tend to earn less then men (the gender wage gap) and the costs of raising children fall
45:1517:101244:20:21:89:310:447:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:primarily upon the mother in case of divorce.45
45:1518:101291:21:20:106:516:426:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We also examined the link between the change in divorce regime and theLFP of married
45:1519:101375:20:20:89:519:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:women.  We found that although the 1940 cohort’s LFP increased by a relativelysmall
45:1520:101458:20:21:89:516:386:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:amount when confronted with a switch to a unilateral divorce regime, the differences in
45:1521:101545:21:20:89:517:365:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:married LFP across the two regimes would be substantially higher if one compared cohorts
45:1522:101633:20:20:89:517:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that always lived in one versus the other regime.  The higher married women’s LFP under
45:1523:101720:20:21:89:516:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a unilateral divorce regime is mostly a response to spouses’ conflicting preferences regarding
45:1524:101814:21:20:89:431:304:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consumption smoothing in the face of endogenously higher divorce risk.
45:1525:101884:20:20:106:515:284:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We explored the robustness of our main results to various features of the calibration
45:1526:101969:20:21:89:517:264:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:procedure.  We experimented with slightly higher and lower Pareto weights for the wife
45:1527:102055:21:20:89:518:243:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(λin the range of 0.2 to 0.4), more generous child support (20 percent), a wider range for
45:1528:102145:20:20:89:517:223:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:childcare costs (40 to 60 percent of average working women’s wages), a different baseline
45:1529:102234:20:21:89:519:203:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:asset split between the husband and the wife (70/30 (30/70) and 60/40 (40/60)). Our overall
45:1530:102325:21:20:89:311:182:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:welfare results remained qualitatively similar.46
45:1531:102374:20:20:106:517:162:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Our model provides a framework in which to analyze the positive and normative impact
45:1532:102458:20:21:89:516:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of policies that affect the process of household formation, from the increased ability to
45:1533:102547:21:15:89:516:121:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:write binding pre-nuptial contracts, to the growing tendency toshare child custody, to
45:1534:102633:15:11:98:498:106:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:45They are also amplified by women’s disutility from working, especially if they have young children
45:1535:102733:11:0:98:244:95:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:46Results are available upon request.
46:1536:102772:0:21:90:517:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the work and marriage incentives provided by the tax code, among others.  The analysis
46:1537:102858:21:20:90:516:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:could be extended in a variety of important ways by, for example, studying other household
46:1538:102948:20:20:90:515:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:bargaining environments (e.g., Lundberg and Pollak (1996)), endogenizing fertility, and
46:1539:103035:20:21:90:515:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:using a richer model of assortative matching, among others.47The model can also be used
46:1540:103122:21:20:90:519:609:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to gain insight into questions related to growth and development that are often ignored,
46:1541:103210:20:20:90:515:589:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:such as how divorce regimes affect savings, the relationship betweenregime preferences and
46:1542:103300:20:21:90:517:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:income, or how marriage and divorce respond to the availability of other credit and insurance
46:1543:103393:21:30:90:482:548:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:mechanisms outside the family or to the security of property rights upon divorce.48

55:1850:117450:11:7:108:501:176:6:g_d0_f5:6:g_d0_f5:F:Note: The first two rows (“MC” and “Unilateral”) for women and men show the average lifetime discounted utility under

56:1854:117924:0:32:90:179:691:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:A  Appendix
56:1855:117935:32:28:90:218:659:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:A.1  Cohorts and LFP
56:1856:117955:28:20:90:515:631:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We use the Current Population Survey from 1962- 2010 to compute labor force participation
56:1857:118044:20:20:90:517:611:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rates.  We construct a synthetic cohort of white women born between 1939-1941and not
56:1858:118128:20:21:90:519:591:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:living in group quarters (“the 1940s cohort”), and compute their LFP as the proportion of
56:1859:118217:21:20:90:515:570:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:women in a particular age span, e.g., 20-24, who report being in the labor force.  At each
56:1860:118307:20:20:90:517:550:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:age, we calculate the proportion of women from the cohort who report being inthe labor
56:1861:118393:20:20:90:515:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:force.  This generates an LFP for each age, which we then average across all ages within
56:1862:118481:20:21:90:517:510:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:an age bracket in order to compute the final LFP for that bracket.  Data is available for
56:1863:118570:21:20:90:517:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the entire period except prior to 1962 when our cohort is 21-23.  To calculateLFP at age
56:1864:118658:20:20:90:517:469:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:20 for our cohort, we use the 1960 census and compute the LFP in the same way as above
56:1865:118744:20:21:90:517:449:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and use that statistic when we average across ages 20-24.  For the relevant statistics for
56:1866:118834:21:20:90:517:428:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:men, our sample consists of men born between 1942-1944 in order to capture theaverage
56:1867:118919:20:20:90:517:408:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:age difference between husbands and wives (approximately 3 years for the 1939-41 cohort
56:1868:119006:20:21:90:518:388:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of women).  Married people are defined as those ?married, with spouse present?, singles
56:1869:119093:21:20:90:517:367:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are those people who report ?never married? whereas divorced people are those who report
56:1870:119181:20:36:90:370:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:their marital status to be either ?divorced? or ?separated?.
56:1871:119241:36:28:90:156:311:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:A.2  Wages
56:1872:119251:28:20:90:519:283:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We compute the gender wage gap using hourly wages from the CPS using the individuals’
56:1873:119336:20:20:90:517:263:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:reported labor income and hours and weeks worked last year.  We use the sample of white
56:1874:119423:20:21:90:517:243:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:men and women who do not live in group quarters with the cohorts defined asabove. Prior
56:1875:119510:21:20:90:516:222:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to 1977, for hours per week, we use the variable which reports the hours worked in the
56:1876:119596:20:20:90:516:202:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:previous week, by intervals; we use the midpoint of the interval. From 1977 onward, we use
56:1877:119686:20:21:90:517:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the variables for “usual hours worked per week” (last year) and the continuous variable for
56:1878:119777:21:20:90:519:161:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:number of weeks worked last year.  Whenever we compute lifetime averages for a variable,
56:1879:119865:20:20:90:519:141:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:we first compute the average of the variable over each year and then averageacross years.
56:1880:119954:20:21:90:516:121:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Sample weights are used throughout (PERWT).  Concerning top-coded observations, we
56:1881:120036:21:0:90:517:100:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:follow the procedure in Katz and Autor (1999).  We multiply all top-coded observations
57:1882:120124:0:21:90:517:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:until 1996 by 1.5. After 1996, top-coded observations in the CPS correspond to the average
57:1883:120214:21:20:90:456:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:value of all top-coded observations, thus we do not impose further treatment.
57:1884:120291:20:20:106:516:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We restrict to full time workers for the gender wage ratio and the correlation between
57:1885:120377:20:21:90:517:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:husband and wife’s earnings. We compute the gender wage ratio as the ratioof the average
57:1886:120465:21:20:90:517:609:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:wage for women versus men amongst full time year round workers aged between20-55. The
57:1887:120550:20:20:90:516:589:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:correlation of income between husband and wife is also computed using couples in which
57:1888:120636:20:21:90:517:569:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:both spouses work full-time year-round in the CPS sample and for women between the ages
57:1889:120723:21:36:90:149:548:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of 20 and 44.
57:1890:120736:36:44:90:249:512:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:A.3  Labor Income Process
57:1891:120761:44:23:209:366:468:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f11:A:lnygt(zt,t) =γg+γ1t+γ2t2+zt
57:1892:120788:23:37:250:402:445:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:A:zt=ρzzt−1+ǫt,  ǫt∼N(0,σǫ)
57:1893:120813:37:20:106:515:408:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f3:A:Age Profiles:We use the pooled sample of PSID for the years 1968-2009, restricted
57:1894:120894:20:20:90:513:388:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to white males who are heads of households.49We exclude individuals in the Latino, SEO
57:1895:120980:20:21:90:515:368:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and immigrant samples.   We also drop observations from people younger than 20 and
57:1896:121062:21:20:90:516:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:people older than 65 years old and those who report being self-employed.  We include only
57:1897:121151:20:20:90:517:327:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:individuals with at least 8 (not necessarily consecutive) observations.  Furthermore, we
57:1898:121239:20:21:90:517:307:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:drop individuals with missing, top-coded and zero earnings and those with zero, missing or
57:1899:121329:21:20:90:516:286:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:more than 5840 annual work hours.  Individuals with changes in log earnings greater than
57:1900:121417:20:20:90:342:266:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:4 or less than -2 are also eliminated from the sample.
57:1901:121471:20:21:106:518:246:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We first construct data on hourly wages (ymt) for men using data on earnings and total
57:1902:121557:21:20:90:518:225:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:hours worked.  We then run the following regression in order to estimate the parameters
57:1903:121644:20:37:90:307:205:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ˆγ1,ˆγ2of the second degree polynomial on age:
57:1904:121690:37:37:222:388:168:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f11:A:lnymt=Dt+γ1aget+γ2age2t+wt
57:1905:121716:37:16:90:252:131:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:whereDtis a set of year dummies.
57:1906:121748:16:14:98:517:115:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:49The Panel Study of Income Dynamics (PSID) is the longest panel survey conducted in the US, starting
57:1907:121849:14:0:90:500:101:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:in 1968.  Interviews were conducted on an annual basis until 1997, and from then onwards, biennially.
58:1908:121952:0:21:106:516:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Given the residualswtfrom the regression above, we estimate the parameters for the
58:1909:122034:21:20:90:518:670:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:persistent shock process using the Minimum Distance Estimator(Chamberlain (1984)).
58:1910:122116:20:20:90:518:650:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The methods of estimating this process are standard in the literature (see e.g. Heathcote,
58:1911:122206:20:37:90:443:630:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Storesletten and Violante (2004) for a detailed description of the method).
58:1912:122281:37:27:90:387:593:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:A.4  Marriage, Divorce, and Remarriage Moments
58:1913:122327:27:20:90:517:566:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We use the 2001 and 2004 waves of Survey of Income and Program Participation (SIPP)
58:1914:122410:20:21:90:515:546:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to compute marriage and divorce rates using the cohort of white women born between
58:1915:122492:21:20:90:522:525:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:1938-1942 (“the augmented 1940s cohort” - we expand the cohort definition here due to
58:1916:122577:20:20:90:517:505:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sample size).  Although the model only begins at age 20, we compute marital statistics as
58:1917:122666:20:21:90:515:485:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of age 18 since a non-negligible proportion of women in the 1940 cohort married between
58:1918:122753:21:20:90:517:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the ages of 18 and 20.  Our sample does not include women who married before the age
58:1919:122837:20:20:90:517:444:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of 18, which accounts for about 9 percent of the women in the 1940 cohort observedin the
58:1920:122925:20:21:90:114:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:SIPP.
58:1921:122930:21:20:106:516:403:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Young vs. old divorce rates are computed as the proportion of all marriages which take
58:1922:123016:20:20:90:516:383:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:place between the ages of 18-34 (18-44 in the case of old) that result in a divorce (or a
58:1923:123105:20:21:90:518:363:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:separation) between the ages of 18-34 (young) or between the ages of 35-44 (old).  First
58:1924:123193:21:20:90:516:342:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:time marriage rates during the different ages are computed as the proportion of all women
58:1925:123282:20:20:90:516:322:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the 1940 cohort in the SIPP who marry for the first time between the agesof 18-34
58:1926:123366:20:21:90:460:302:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(young) and those who marry for the first time during the ages of 34-44 (old).
58:1927:123444:21:20:106:515:281:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The probability of divorcing before the 11th anniversary conditional on having been
58:1928:123527:20:20:89:517:261:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:married for 5 years is computed as the proportion of of marriages that take placewhen the
58:1929:123616:20:20:89:517:241:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:woman is between the ages of 18-34 which end after their 5th anniversary butbefore their
58:1930:123704:20:21:89:168:221:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:11th anniversary.
58:1931:123721:21:20:106:517:200:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In order to compute the truncated divorce duration and since the model assumes that
58:1932:123804:20:20:89:517:180:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:marital transitions end at age 44, we choose 44 as the terminal age with which wecompute
58:1933:123892:20:21:89:521:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f9:B:the truncated duration.  Thus, for a given marriage that ended when the woman wasx
58:1934:123974:21:20:89:518:139:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:years old, if we do not observe her remarrying before the age of 44, the divorce duration is
58:1935:124066:20:0:89:210:119:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:calculated as 44 minusx.
59:1936:124092:0:28:90:164:691:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:A.5  Fertility
59:1937:124106:28:20:90:516:663:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Since only a negligible proportion of never married women in the 1940 cohort have children
59:1938:124196:20:20:90:518:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:while single, we assume that single women do not receive fertility shocks in the model.
59:1939:124283:20:21:90:516:623:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We also assume that divorced women do not have more children unless they remarry.  The
59:1940:124369:21:20:90:516:602:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:timing of fertility shocks for married women is as follows. In the first period, married women
59:1941:124463:20:20:90:515:582:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:receive either 0 or 1 child; letp1denote the probability of a non-zero value.  In the second
59:1942:124555:20:21:90:516:562:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:period, married women can receive either 0, 1 or 2 children; letp12,p22denote the probability
59:1943:124648:21:20:90:516:541:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of receiving either 1 or 2 children (and thus the probability of receiving no children in period
59:1944:124744:20:20:90:515:521:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:2 equals 1 minus the sum ofp12andp22).  Finally, in period 3, a woman receives 1 child
59:1945:124830:20:21:90:517:501:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:with probabilityp3and zero otherwise. The probabilitiesp1,p12,p22,p3are set to match the
59:1946:124918:21:20:90:515:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:proportion of women who have children under the age of 5 in the CPS data during each
59:1947:125002:20:20:90:516:460:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the corresponding age brackets: (i) 68.0% between the ages of 20-24, (ii) 89.5% during
59:1948:125091:20:21:90:516:440:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:25-29, (iii) 93.3% during 30-34 - and (iv) in order to match the average number ofchildren
59:1949:125181:21:20:90:522:419:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for women of the 1940 cohort (2.4).  The latter is computed from the 1980 Census by
59:1950:125264:20:20:90:516:399:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:calculating the average number of own children in the household for women in the 1940
59:1951:125349:20:37:90:120:379:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:cohort.
59:1952:125356:37:27:90:255:342:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:A.6  Consumption Deflator:
59:1953:125382:27:20:90:516:315:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We use an altered McClements scale (e(kt;s)) to deflate household consumption. Table A.1
59:1954:125470:20:24:90:409:295:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:reproduces the original McClements scale normalized for one adult.
59:1955:125536:24:23:235:371:271:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Table A.1: McClements Scale
59:1956:125563:23:10:332:387:248:8:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f3:F:+1 child, by age:
59:1957:125580:10:13:147:461:238:8:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f3:F:1 adult  2 adults+ 1 adult0 - 12- 45-78-10    11-12   13-15   16-18
59:1958:125647:13:47:157:462:225:8:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f3:F:11.64+0.75+ 0.148  +0.295  + 0.344  +0.377  +0.41  +0.443  +0.59
59:1959:125711:47:20:106:515:178:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Since we have 5 year periods, and our children are aged 0-4, 5-9, 10-14, 15-20, we weigh
59:1960:125799:20:21:90:522:158:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the scale accordingly. For example, a child aged 0-4 adds: 0.4(0.148)+0.6(0.295) = 0.2362.
59:1961:125889:21:20:106:521:137:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f9:A:The scalee(kt;s) is constructed using the number of adults in the household (1 ifs=S
59:1962:125973:20:0:89:475:117:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:or,Dand 2 ifs=M) and the number of children with their respective ages (kt).
60:1963:126051:0:28:90:175:691:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:A.7  Pensions:
60:1964:126065:28:20:90:515:663:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:To compute retirement benefits for a model household, we modify the approach used in
60:1965:126149:20:20:90:518:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Heathcote, Storesletten and Violante (2010) in order to avoid keeping track ofan individual’s
60:1966:126242:20:21:90:516:623:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:average earnings over their lifecycle.  More specifically, we take each agent’s last observed
60:1967:126335:21:20:90:517:602:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:earnings which we denote byyT(note that this isyTRfor men and the last period worked for
60:1968:126423:20:20:90:516:582:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a woman) and compute social security benefits as follows: 90% ofyTup to a first threshold
60:1969:126512:20:21:89:517:562:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:equal to 0.38 ̄yT, where  ̄yTis the average observed earnings in the economy during the last
60:1970:126604:21:20:89:513:541:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:period, plus 32% ofyTfrom this bendpoint to a higher bendpoint equal to 1.59 ̄yT, plus 15%
60:1971:126694:20:20:89:517:521:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the remainingyTexceeding this last bendpoint.  For married households, this process is
60:1972:126783:20:21:90:517:501:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:performed for both the husband and the wife; the household total benefits are the highest
60:1973:126872:21:36:90:420:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of either the sum of their benefits or 1.5 times the husband’s benefits.
60:1974:126944:36:31:90:167:444:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:A.8  Figures:
60:1975:126957:31:107:170:434:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Figure A.1: A typical work period for a divorced woman
